## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

# Debug Q&A: Cilium eBPF Fault Isolation

**Repository:** github.com/sg-evals/cilium--a2f97aa8 (mirror of cilium/cilium)
**Task Type:** Debug Q&A (investigation only — no code changes)

## Background

Cilium is a Kubernetes CNI (Container Network Interface) plugin that uses eBPF (Extended Berkeley Packet Filter) programs to enforce network policies and route traffic. In a multi-node Kubernetes cluster, each node runs its own Cilium agent which compiles, loads, and attaches eBPF programs to enforce policies.

## Behavior Observation

**What happens:** When an eBPF program fails to compile or load on one Kubernetes node (e.g., due to a kernel verifier rejection, compilation error, or incompatible kernel features), the other nodes in the cluster continue to enforce their network policies normally. The failing node may log errors or degrade to a fallback mode, but the failure doesn't propagate cluster-wide.

**Why is this notable?** Many distributed systems that rely on shared state or centralized configuration can fail cluster-wide when one node encounters a problem. Cilium's architecture ensures that eBPF datapath failures are isolated to the affected node.

## Questions

Answer ALL of the following questions to explain this behavior:

### Q1: Per-Node eBPF Lifecycle

How are eBPF programs compiled, loaded, and attached on each node independently?
- What component is responsible for compiling eBPF programs on each node?
- How does node-specific configuration (kernel version, enabled features, etc.) affect compilation?
- At what point in the lifecycle does the eBPF program become node-local vs. cluster-wide?

### Q2: Deployment Architecture

How does Cilium's deployment model ensure per-node isolation?
- How is the Cilium agent deployed across the cluster (DaemonSet, static pods, etc.)?
- What happens when one node's Cilium agent fails to initialize its eBPF programs?
- How does the control plane vs. data plane split contribute to isolation?

### Q3: Policy Distribution vs. Enforcement

Cilium network policies are cluster-wide resources (CRDs), but enforcement is per-node. How does this work?
- How are CiliumNetworkPolicy resources distributed to each node?
- What component on each node translates policies into eBPF bytecode?
- Why doesn't a compilation failure on one node block policy distribution to other nodes?

### Q4: eBPF Map Scoping and State Isolation

eBPF programs use maps (hash tables, arrays) to store state. How is map state isolated across nodes?
- Are eBPF maps node-local or cluster-wide?
- What mechanisms (BPF filesystem pinning, namespaces) ensure map isolation?
- If a node fails to create or update a map, how does that affect other nodes' packet processing?

## Output Requirements

I am thinking...: I now have enough information to write a comprehensive answer to all four questions. Let me organize what I've found:

**Q1: Per-Node eBPF Lifecycle**
- The `loader` struct in `pkg/datapath/loader/loader.go` is the central component responsible for compiling, loading, and attaching eBPF programs on each node.
- Compilation happens via `compile()` in `pkg/datapath/loader/compile.go`, which invokes `clang` with node-specific flags:
  - `getBPFCPU()` probes the local kernel for ISA support (v1/v2/v3) using `probes.HaveV3ISA()`, `probes.HaveV2ISA()` - this is node-specific
  - `-D__NR_CPUS__` is set from `ebpf.PossibleCPU()` - node-specific
  - Include paths from `option.Config.BpfDir` and `option.Config.StateDir` contain node-specific headers
- The `objectCache` in `pkg/datapath/loader/cache.go` caches compiled templates per-node. `fetchOrCompile()` hashes the endpoint configuration and node config to determine if recompilation is needed.
- `ReloadDatapath()` in `loader.go` is the main entry point: it calls `templateCache.fetchOrCompile()` then `reloadEndpoint()` or `reloadHostEndpoint()`.
- The eBPF program becomes node-local at the point of `bpf.LoadAndAssign()` in `reloadEndpoint()` - this loads the ELF into the kernel via the local kernel's BPF syscall.
- Node-specific configuration is written via `writeNodeConfigHeader()` (writes `node_config.h`) and `writeNetdevHeader()` (writes `netdev_config.h`).

**Q2: Deployment Architecture**
- Cilium is deployed as a DaemonSet (confirmed in `Documentation/network/kubernetes/concepts.rst` lines 19-23: "A DaemonSet resource: describes the Cilium pod that is deployed to each Kubernetes node. This pod runs the cilium-agent and associated daemons.")

392026-03-08T22:17:59.664029agentmessage-
The investigation document has been written to `/logs/agent/investigation.md`. Here is a summary of the findings:

---

## Summary of Findings

### Q1: Per-Node eBPF Lifecycle

The `loader` struct (`pkg/datapath/loader/loader.go`) is the component responsible for compiling, loading, and attaching eBPF programs on each node. Compilation is performed by `compile()` in `pkg/datapath/loader/compile.go`, which invokes `clang` with node-specific flags:

- **CPU ISA**: `getBPFCPU()` probes the local kernel via `probes.HaveV3ISA()` / `probes.HaveV2ISA()` to select `-mcpu=v1/v2/v3`
- **CPU count**: `ebpf.PossibleCPU()` injects `-D__NR_CPUS__=<n>` from the local node
- **Node config headers**: `writeNodeConfigHeader()` and `writeNetdevHeader()` write `node_config.h` / `netdev_config.h` with node-specific IPs, MTU, and feature flags

The program becomes node-local at `bpf.LoadAndAssign()` inside `reloadEndpoint()` (loader.go:511), which issues the `bpf(BPF_PROG_LOAD)` syscall to the **local** kernel's verifier and JIT compiler.

### Q2: Deployment Architecture

Cilium is deployed as a **DaemonSet** — one `cilium-agent` per node, each running independently. When one node's agent fails to initialize eBPF programs, `realizeBPFState()` (bpf.go:548) returns the error locally, `LogStatus(BPF, Failure, ...)` marks only that endpoint as failed, and `startRegenerationFailureHandler()` (policy.go:908) starts a per-node retry controller. The `compilationLock` is a node-local `RWMutex` with no cross-node effect. The control plane (K8s API/etcd) distributes policy CRDs cluster-wide, but the data plane (eBPF programs and maps) is entirely local to each node's kernel.

### Q3: Policy Distribution vs. Enforcement

Each node's agent independently watches CNP/CCNP/KNP resources via `startK8sPolicyW
... (truncated)

to attach the host endpoint\\n175: // programs to different interfaces.\\n176: func hostRewrites(cfg *datapath.LocalNodeConfiguration, ep datapath.Endpoint, ifName string) (map[string]uint64, map[string]string, error) {\\n177: \\topts := ELFVariableSubstitutions(ep)\\n178: \\tstrings := ELFMapSubstitutions(ep)\\n179: \\n180: \\tiface, err := safenetlink.LinkByName(ifName)\\n181: \\tif err \\treturn opts, strings, nil\\n224: }\\n225: \\n226: func isObsoleteDev(dev string, devices []string) bool {\\n227: \\t// exclude devices we never attach to/from_netdev to.\\n228: \\tfor _, prefix := Let me organize what I've found:\n\n**Q1: Per-Node eBPF Lifecycle**\n- The `loader` struct in `pkg/datapath/loader/loader.go` is the central component responsible for compiling, loading, and attaching eBPF programs on each node.\n- Compilation happens via `compile()` in `pkg/datapath/loader/compile.go`, which invokes `clang` with node-specific flags:\n  - `getBPFCPU()` probes the local kernel for ISA support (v1/v2/v3) using `probes.HaveV3ISA()`, `probes.HaveV2ISA()` - this is node-specific\n  - `-D__NR_CPUS__` is set from `ebpf.PossibleCPU()` - node-specific\n  - Include paths from `option.Config.BpfDir` and `option.Config.StateDir` contain node-specific headers\n- The `objectCache` in `pkg/datapath/loader/cache.go` caches compiled templates per-node. `fetchOrCompile()` hashes the endpoint configuration and node config to determine if recompilation is needed.\n- `ReloadDatapath()` in `loader.go` is the main entry point: it calls `templateCache.fetchOrCompile()` then `reloadEndpoint()` or `reloadHostEndpoint()`.\n- The eBPF program becomes node-local at the point of `bpf.LoadAndAssign()` in `reloadEndpoint()` - this loads the ELF into the kernel via the local kernel's BPF syscall.\n- Node-specific configuration is written via `writeNodeConfigHeader()` (writes `node_config.h`) and `writeNetdevHeader()` (writes `netdev_config.h`).\n\n**Q2: Deployment Architecture**\n- Cilium is deployed as a DaemonSet (confirmed in `Documentation/network/kubernetes/concepts.rst` lines 19-23: \"A DaemonSet resource: describes the Cilium pod that is deployed to each Kubernetes node. This pod runs the cilium-agent and associated daemons.\")\n- Each node runs its own independent `cilium-agent` process with its own `loader` instance, `objectCache`, and `compilationLock`.\n- When one node's agent fails to initialize eBPF programs, the failure is contained to that node. The `startRegenerationFailureHandler()` in `pkg/endpoint/policy.go` (lines 908-944) creates a controller that retries regeneration on failure - this is per-endpoint, per-node.\n- The control plane (Kubernetes API server, etcd) distributes policy CRDs cluster-wide, but the data plane (eBPF programs, maps) is entirely local to each node.\n- The `compilationLock` in `loader.go` is a node-local mutex that serializes base program compilation with endpoint compilation on that node only.\n- `hostDpInitializedOnce` and `hostDpInitialized` channel in `loader.go` (lines 81-82) signal when the host datapath is ready on the local node.\n\n**Q3: Policy Distribution vs. Enforcement**\n- CiliumNetworkPolicy (CNP) resources are cluster-wide Kubernetes CRDs.\n- Each node's agent watches these CRDs via `pkg/policy/k8s/cell.go` - the `startK8sPolicyWatcher()` function starts a per-node watcher that translates CNP/CCNP/KNP resources into Cilium's internal policy representation.\n- The `policyWatcher` in `pkg/policy/k8s/cilium_network_policy.go` calls `p.policyImporter.UpdatePolicy()` to update the local policy repository.\n- The local `Repository` in `pkg/policy/repository.go` stores the policy rules in-memory on each node.\n- The `policyCache` in `pkg/policy/distillery.go` resolves policies per-identity using `updateSelectorPolicy()` \u2192 `cache.repo.resolvePolicyLocked()`.\n- `selectorPolicy.DistillPolicy()` in `pkg/policy/resolve.go` converts the selector-based policy into concrete `EndpointPolicy` with a `policyMapState`.\n- The `Endpoint.regenerateBPF()` in `pkg/endpoint/bpf.go` calls `realizeBPFState()` which calls `e.owner.Orchestrator().ReloadDatapath()` - this is the point where policy becomes eBPF bytecode on the local node.\n- A compilation failure on one node returns an error from `ReloadDatapath()` (line 566-571 in bpf.go), which is logged and the endpoint is marked as failed. The K8s watcher on other nodes continues independently - they have their own policy repositories and their own compilation pipelines.\n- `CiliumNetworkPolicyNodeStatus` in `pkg/k8s/apis/cilium.io/v2/cnp_types.go` tracks per-node policy status - each node reports its own status independently.\n\n**Q4: eBPF Map Scoping and State Isolation**\n- eBPF maps are node-local. They are pinned to the BPF filesystem (bpffs) on each node.\n- `bpf.TCGlobalsPath()` returns `<bpffs>/tc/globals` (typically `/sys/fs/bpf/tc/globals`) - this is the host's local bpffs.\n- `bpf.CiliumPath()` returns `<bpffs>/cilium` - also local.\n- Per-endpoint policy maps are named `cilium_policy_v2_<endpoint-id>` (from `policymap.MapName = \"cilium_policy_v2_\"` in `pkg/maps/policymap/policymap.go`).\n- `policymap.OpenOrCreate(path)` creates/opens the map at a local path like `/sys/fs/bpf/tc/globals/cilium_policy_v2_00001`.\n- `bpf.LocalMapPath(name, id)` in `pkg/bpf/bpffs_linux.go` constructs the path as `<TCGlobalsPath>/<name><id>` - entirely local.\n- Per-endpoint bpffs directories: `bpffsEndpointDir()` returns `/sys/fs/bpf/cilium/endpoints/<endpoint-id>` (from `pkg/datapath/loader/paths.go`).\n- The `lxcmap` (`cilium_lxc`) is a node-local hash map that maps endpoint IPs to endpoint info.\n- If a node fails to create or update a map, the error is returned from `lxcmap.WriteEndpoint()` (line 473 in bpf.go) or `policymap.OpenOrCreate()`, causing only that endpoint's regeneration to fail on that node. Other nodes' maps are completely independent - they live in different kernel instances.\n- The BPF filesystem is mounted per-node (each node has its own `/sys/fs/bpf`), so there is no shared state between nodes at the map level.\n- Global maps like `cilium_call_policy` (PolicyCallMapName) and `cilium_egresscall_policy` (PolicyEgressCallMapName) are also node-local - they exist in each node's kernel.\n"

It owns a `templateCache *objectCache`, a `compilationLock`, and a `configWriter`. The public entry point is `loader.ReloadDatapath()` (lines 700\u2013732), which is called per-endpoint during regeneration.\n\nCompilation itself is performed by the `compile()` function in `pkg/datapath/loader/compile.go` (lines 170\u2013257). It invokes `clang` as a subprocess with the source files `bpf_lxc.c` (endpoint programs) or `bpf_host.c` (host programs), defined as `epProg` and `hostEpProg` (lines 117\u2013131).\n\n### How node-specific configuration affects compilation\n\nThree mechanisms make compilation node-specific:\n\n1. **CPU ISA probing** (`getBPFCPU()`, `compile.go` lines 135\u2013157): At startup, the agent probes the local kernel using `probes.HaveV3ISA()` and `probes.HaveV2ISA()` to select the BPF CPU target (`-mcpu=v1/v2/v3`). This flag is passed directly to `clang` (line 192), so nodes with different kernel versions produce different object files.\n\n2. **CPU count** (`compile.go` line 191): `ebpf.PossibleCPU()` is called at compile time and injected as `-D__NR_CPUS__=<n>`. This is node-local.\n\n3. **Node configuration headers**: `loader.writeNodeConfigHeader()` (`base.go` lines 63\u201375) writes `node_config.h` containing node-specific values (IP addresses, MTU, feature flags). `loader.writeNetdevHeader()` (`base.go` lines 46\u201361) writes `netdev_config.h`. These headers are included by the BPF C source files via the `-I<dir.State>` and `-I<dir.Runtime>` flags passed to `clang` (`compile.go` lines 177\u2013181).\n\nThe `objectCache.build()` function (`cache.go` lines 115\u2013158) writes the endpoint-specific header via `o.ConfigWriter.WriteEndpointConfig()` (line 141) before calling `compileDatapath()` (line 146). The cache key is a hash of the endpoint configuration and node configuration (`objectCache.fetchOrCompile()`, `cache.go` lines 167\u2013222), so any node-specific difference produces a distinct compiled object.\n\n### When the eBPF program becomes node-local\n\nThe program becomes node-local at the point of `bpf.LoadAndAssign()` in `reloadEndpoint()` (`loader.go` lines 511\u2013584) or `reloadHostEndpoint()` (lines 319\u2013334). `LoadAndAssign` issues the `bpf(BPF_PROG_LOAD, ...)` syscall to the **local** kernel, which runs the verifier and JIT-compiles the bytecode. After this call, the program exists only in the local kernel's memory. The subsequent `attachSKBProgram()` calls (e.g., line 547) attach the loaded program to the local network interface via TC or TCX hooks.\n\n---\n\n## Q2: Deployment Architecture\n\n### Cilium agent deployment model\n\nCilium is deployed as a **DaemonSet** (`Documentation/network/kubernetes/concepts.rst`, lines 19\u201323): \"A DaemonSet resource: describes the Cilium pod that is deployed to each Kubernetes node. This pod runs the cilium-agent and associated daemons.\" This guarantees exactly one `cilium-agent` process per node, each running independently with its own in-process state.\n\n### What happens when one node's agent fails to initialize eBPF programs\n\nFailure is contained to the affected node through several mechanisms:\n\n1. **Per-endpoint error isolation**: `Endpoint.realizeBPFState()` (`pkg/endpoint/bpf.go` lines 548\u2013586) calls `e.owner.Orchestrator().ReloadDatapath()`. If this returns an error (line 567\u2013571), the error is logged locally (`e.getLogger().WithError(err).Error(\"Error while reloading endpoint BPF program\")`) and returned up the call stack to `regenerateBPF()` (line 465\u2013468), which returns it to `regenerate()` in `pkg/endpoint/policy.go`.\n\n2. **Local status logging**: `pkg/endpoint/policy.go` line 600 calls `e.LogStatus(BPF, Failure, \"Error regenerating endpoint: \"+err.Error())`, marking only the local endpoint as failed.\n\n3. **Automatic retry**: `startRegenerationFailureHandler()` (`pkg/endpoint/policy.go` lines 908\u2013944) registers a per-endpoint controller that listens on `e.regenFailedChan` and retries regeneration with `RegenerateWithDatapath` level every 1\u20132 seconds. This retry loop is entirely local to the failing node.\n\n4. **No cluster-wide propagation**: The `compilationLock` (`loader.go` line 86) is a node-local `RWMutex`. Endpoint regeneration takes a read lock (`pkg/endpoint/bpf.go` line 396: `e.owner.GetCompilationLock().RLock()`), and base program compilation takes a write lock (`base.go` line 392). These locks are in-process and have no effect on other nodes.\n\n### Control plane vs. data plane split\n\nThe **control plane** (Kubernetes API server, etcd, Cilium operator) distributes policy CRDs cluster-wide. Each node's agent independently watches these CRDs and maintains its own in-memory policy repository (`pkg/policy/repository.go`). The **data plane** (eBPF programs, BPF maps) is entirely local to each node's kernel. A failure in the data plane on one node (e.g., kernel verifier rejection) does not affect the control plane's ability to distribute policies to other nodes, nor does it affect other nodes' data planes.\n\n---\n\n## Q3: Policy Distribution vs. Enforcement\n\n### How CiliumNetworkPolicy resources are distributed to each node\n\nEach node's `cilium-agent` runs its own Kubernetes informer/watcher. The `pkg/policy/k8s/cell.go` module (lines 36\u201348) starts `startK8sPolicyWatcher()`, which watches all policy-related K8s resources: `KubernetesNetworkPolicy` (KNP), `CiliumNetworkPolicy` (CNP), `ClusterwideCiliumNetworkPolicy` (CCNP), and `CiliumCIDRGroup` (CCG). The `policyWatcher` in `pkg/policy/k8s/cilium_network_policy.go` translates CNP objects into Cilium's internal `api.Rules` and calls `p.policyImporter.UpdatePolicy()` (line 186) to update the local policy repository. This is a **pull model**: each node independently fetches and processes policy updates from the Kubernetes API server.\n\n### What component translates policies into eBPF bytecode\n\nThe translation pipeline is:\n\n1. **`pkg/policy/repository.go` (`Repository`)**: Stores raw policy rules. `resolvePolicyLocked()` evaluates rules against an identity to produce a `selectorPolicy`.\n\n2. **`pkg/policy/distillery.go` (`policyCache`)**: `updateSelectorPolicy()` (lines 73\u2013102) calls `cache.repo.resolvePolicyLocked()` and caches the result per identity.\n\n3. **`pkg/policy/resolve.go` (`selectorPolicy.DistillPolicy()`)** (lines 160\u2013205): Converts the selector-based policy into a concrete `EndpointPolicy` with a `policyMapState` (a map of `Key \u2192 MapStateEntry`). This is the datapath-friendly representation.\n\n4. **`pkg/endpoint/bpf.go` (`Endpoint.regenerateBPF()`)**: Calls `realizeBPFState()` (line 465), which calls `e.owner.Orchestrator().ReloadDatapath()` (line 566). This invokes `loader.ReloadDatapath()`, which compiles (if needed) and loads the eBPF program into the local kernel.\n\n5. **`pkg/endpoint/bpf.go` (`Endpoint.policyMapSync()`)** (lines 534\u2013546): After loading the program, syncs the `EndpointPolicy.policyMapState` into the kernel BPF map via `syncPolicyMap()` or `syncPolicyMapWith()`.\n\n### Why a compilation failure on one node doesn't block policy distribution to other nodes\n\nPolicy distribution (step 1 above) and policy enforcement (steps 4\u20135) are **decoupled**. The K8s watcher on each node independently updates the local `Repository`. A compilation failure in `ReloadDatapath()` on node A returns an error only to node A's `regenerateBPF()` call. Node B's watcher continues to receive CNP updates from the API server, and node B's `regenerateBPF()` runs independently in node B's process. There is no shared compilation state, no distributed lock, and no cross-node signaling in the compilation path.\n\nPer-node policy status is tracked independently via `CiliumNetworkPolicyNodeStatus` (`pkg/k8s/apis/cilium.io/v2/cnp_types.go` lines 90\u201396): each node reports its own `OK` and `Enforcing` fields to the CNP status subresource, so a failure on one node is visible in the CNP status without affecting other nodes' enforcement.\n\n---\n\n## Q4: eBPF Map Scoping and State Isolation\n\n### Are eBPF maps node-local or cluster-wide?\n\neBPF maps are **strictly node-local**. They exist in the kernel of the node where they were created. There is no mechanism for eBPF maps to span multiple nodes.\n\n### BPF filesystem pinning and namespaces\n\nMaps are pinned to the BPF filesystem (bpffs) on each node:\n\n- **`bpf.TCGlobalsPath()`** (`pkg/bpf/bpffs_linux.go` lines 49\u201354): Returns `<bpffs>/tc/globals` (default: `/sys/fs/bpf/tc/globals`). Global maps like `cilium_lxc` (lxcmap), `cilium_call_policy`, and `cilium_egresscall_policy` are pinned here.\n\n- **`bpf.CiliumPath()`** (`pkg/bpf/bpffs_linux.go` lines 56\u201360): Returns `<bpffs>/cilium`. Per-endpoint and per-device directories are created under this path.\n\n- **Per-endpoint directories**: `bpffsEndpointDir()` (`pkg/datapath/loader/paths.go` lines 63\u201365) returns `/sys/fs/bpf/cilium/endpoints/<endpoint-id>`. Per-endpoint bpf_link objects (for TCX attachment) are pinned in `bpffsEndpointLinksDir()` (lines 73\u201375).\n\n- **Per-device directories**: `bpffsDeviceDir()` (`paths.go` lines 29\u201336) returns `/sys/fs/bpf/cilium/devices/<device-name>`.\n\n- **Per-endpoint policy maps**: Named `cilium_policy_v2_<id>` (from `policymap.MapName = \"cilium_policy_v2_\"`, `pkg/maps/policymap/policymap.go` line 34). The path is constructed by `bpf.LocalMapPath(policymap.MapName, e.ID)` (`pkg/endpoint/bpf.go` line 88), which resolves to `/sys/fs/bpf/tc/globals/cilium_policy_v2_<id>`. `policymap.OpenOrCreate(path)` (lines 487\u2013491) creates or opens this map on the local node only.\n\n- **Global call maps**: `cilium_call_policy` and `cilium_egresscall_policy` (program arrays, `policymap.go` lines 25\u201329) are created by `policymap.InitCallMaps()` (lines 514\u2013536) on each node independently.\n\n- **lxcmap** (`cilium_lxc`): A node-local hash map (`pkg/maps/lxcmap/lxcmap.go` lines 36\u201348) mapping endpoint IPs to endpoint metadata. Written by `lxcmap.WriteEndpoint()` (`pkg/endpoint/bpf.go` line 473).\n\nThe bpffs is mounted per-node (each Linux kernel has its own `/sys/fs/bpf` namespace). The `CheckOrMountFS()` function (`pkg/bpf/bpffs_linux.go` lines 295\u2013301) mounts bpffs on the local node at startup.\n\n### How a map failure on one node affects other nodes\n\nIt does not. If `lxcmap.WriteEndpoint()` fails on node A (line 473\u2013477 in `pkg/endpoint/bpf.go`), the error is returned from `regenerateBPF()` and the endpoint on node A is marked as failed. Node B's `lxcmap` is a completely separate kernel object in node B's kernel. Similarly, if `policymap.OpenOrCreate()` fails on node A, only node A's endpoint loses its policy map; node B's policy maps are unaffected.\n\nThe `syncPolicyMapWithDump()` function (`pkg/endpoint/bpf.go` lines 1525\u20131574) runs periodically on each node to reconcile the in-memory policy state with the kernel map. If the map cannot be dumped, it attempts to close and reopen it (lines 1545\u20131553). This recovery logic is entirely local to the node where the failure occurred.\n\n---\n\n## Evidence\n\n| File | Lines | Relevance |\n|------|-------|-----------|\n| `pkg/datapath/loader/loader.go` | "# Cilium eBPF Fault Isolation\n\n## Q1: Per-Node eBPF Lifecycle\n\n### Component responsible for compiling eBPF programs\n\nThe `loader` struct in `pkg/datapath/loader/loader.go` (lines 74\u201389) is the central component. It owns a `templateCache *objectCache`, a `compilationLock`, and a `configWriter`. The public entry point is `loader.ReloadDatapath()` (lines 700\u2013732), which is called per-endpoint during regeneration.\n\nCompilation itself is performed by the `compile()` function in `pkg/datapath/loader/compile.go` (lines 170\u2013257). It invokes `clang` as a subprocess with the source files `bpf_lxc.c` (endpoint programs) or `bpf_host.c` (host programs), defined as `epProg` and `hostEpProg` (lines 117\u2013131).\n\n### How node-specific configuration affects compilation\n\nThree mechanisms make compilation node-specific:\n\n1. **CPU ISA probing** (`getBPFCPU()`, `compile.go` lines 135\u2013157): At startup, the agent probes the local kernel using `probes.HaveV3ISA()` and `probes.HaveV2ISA()` to select the BPF CPU target (`-mcpu=v1/v2/v3`). This flag is passed directly to `clang` (line 192), so nodes with different kernel versions produce different object files.\n\n2. **CPU count** (`compile.go` line 191): `ebpf.PossibleCPU()` is called at compile time and injected as `-D__NR_CPUS__=<n>`. This is node-local.\n\n3. **Node configuration headers**: `loader.writeNodeConfigHeader()` (`base.go` lines 63\u201375) writes `node_config.h` containing node-specific values (IP addresses, MTU, feature flags). `loader.writeNetdevHeader()` (`base.go` lines 46\u201361) writes `netdev_config.h`. These headers are included by the BPF C source files via the `-I<dir.State>` and `-I<dir.Runtime>` flags passed to `clang` (`compile.go` lines 177\u2013181).\n\nThe `objectCache.build()` function (`cache.go` lines 115\u2013158) writes the endpoint-specific header via `o.ConfigWriter.WriteEndpointConfig()` (line 141) before calling `compileDatapath()` (line 146). The cache key is a hash of the endpoint configuration and node configuration (`objectCache.fetchOrCompile()`, `cache.go` lines 167\u2013222), so any node-specific difference produces a distinct compiled object.\n\n### When the eBPF program becomes node-local\n\nThe program becomes node-local at the point of `bpf.LoadAndAssign()` in `reloadEndpoint()` (`loader.go` lines 511\u2013584) or `reloadHostEndpoint()` (lines 319\u2013334). `LoadAndAssign` issues the `bpf(BPF_PROG_LOAD, ...)` syscall to the **local** kernel, which runs the verifier and JIT-compiles the bytecode. After this call, the program exists only in the local kernel's memory. The subsequent `attachSKBProgram()` calls (e.g., line 547) attach the loaded program to the local network interface via TC or TCX hooks.\n\n---\n\n## Q2: Deployment Architecture\n\n### Cilium agent deployment model\n\nCilium is deployed as a **DaemonSet** (`Documentation/network/kubernetes/concepts.rst`, lines 19\u201323): \"A DaemonSet resource: describes the Cilium pod that is deployed to each Kubernetes node. This pod runs the cilium-agent and associated daemons.\" This guarantees exactly one `cilium-agent` process per node, each running independently with its own in-process state.\n\n### What happens when one node's agent fails to initialize eBPF programs\n\nFailure is contained to the affected node through several mechanisms:\n\n1. **Per-endpoint error isolation**: `Endpoint.realizeBPFState()` (`pkg/endpoint/bpf.go` lines 548\u2013586) calls `e.owner.Orchestrator().ReloadDatapath()`. If this returns an error (line 567\u2013571), the error is logged locally (`e.getLogger().WithError(err).Error(\"Error while reloading endpoint BPF program\")`) and returned up the call stack to `regenerateBPF()` (line 465\u2013468), which returns it to `regenerate()` in `pkg/endpoint/policy.go`.\n\n2. **Local status logging**: `pkg/endpoint/policy.go` line 600 calls `e.LogStatus(BPF, Failure, \"Error regenerating endpoint: \"+err.Error())`, marking only the local endpoint as failed.\n\n3. **Automatic retry**: `startRegenerationFailureHandler()` (`pkg/endpoint/policy.go` lines 908\u2013944) registers a per-endpoint controller that listens on `e.regenFailedChan` and retries regeneration with `RegenerateWithDatapath` level every 1\u20132 seconds. This retry loop is entirely local to the failing node.\n\n4. **No cluster-wide propagation**: The `compilationLock` (`loader.go` line 86) is a node-local `RWMutex`. Endpoint regeneration takes a read lock (`pkg/endpoint/bpf.go` line 396: `e.owner.GetCompilationLock().RLock()`), and base program compilation takes a write lock (`base.go` line 392). These locks are in-process and have no effect on other nodes.\n\n### Control plane vs. data plane split\n\nThe **control plane** (Kubernetes API server, etcd, Cilium operator) distributes policy CRDs cluster-wide. Each node's agent independently watches these CRDs and maintains its own in-memory policy repository (`pkg/policy/repository.go`). The **data plane** (eBPF programs, BPF maps) is entirely local to each node's kernel. A failure in the data plane on one node (e.g., kernel verifier rejection) does not affect the control plane's ability to distribute policies to other nodes, nor does it affect other nodes' data planes.\n\n---\n\n## Q3: Policy Distribution vs. Enforcement\n\n### How CiliumNetworkPolicy resources are distributed to each node\n\nEach node's `cilium-agent` runs its own Kubernetes informer/watcher. The `pkg/policy/k8s/cell.go` module (lines 36\u201348) starts `startK8sPolicyWatcher()`, which watches all policy-related K8s resources: `KubernetesNetworkPolicy` (KNP), `CiliumNetworkPolicy` (CNP), `ClusterwideCiliumNetworkPolicy` (CCNP), and `CiliumCIDRGroup` (CCG). The `policyWatcher` in `pkg/policy/k8s/cilium_network_policy.go` translates CNP objects into Cilium's internal `api.Rules` and calls `p.policyImporter.UpdatePolicy()` (line 186) to update the local policy repository. This is a **pull model**: each node independently fetches and processes policy updates from the Kubernetes API server.\n\n### What component translates policies into eBPF bytecode\n\nThe translation pipeline is:\n\n1. **`pkg/policy/repository.go` (`Repository`)**: Stores raw policy rules. `resolvePolicyLocked()` evaluates rules against an identity to produce a `selectorPolicy`.\n\n2. **`pkg/policy/distillery.go` (`policyCache`)**: `updateSelectorPolicy()` (lines 73\u2013102) calls `cache.repo.resolvePolicyLocked()` and caches the result per identity.\n\n3. **`pkg/policy/resolve.go` (`selectorPolicy.DistillPolicy()`)** (lines 160\u2013205): Converts the selector-based policy into a concrete `EndpointPolicy` with a `policyMapState` (a map of `Key \u2192 MapStateEntry`). This is the datapath-friendly representation.\n\n4. **`pkg/endpoint/bpf.go` (`Endpoint.regenerateBPF()`)**: Calls `realizeBPFState()` (line 465), which calls `e.owner.Orchestrator().ReloadDatapath()` (line 566). This invokes `loader.ReloadDatapath()`, which compiles (if needed) and loads the eBPF program into the local kernel.\n\n5. **`pkg/endpoint/bpf.go` (`Endpoint.policyMapSync()`)** (lines 534\u2013546): After loading the program, syncs the `EndpointPolicy.policyMapState` into the kernel BPF map via `syncPolicyMap()` or `syncPolicyMapWith()`.\n\n### Why a compilation failure on one node doesn't block policy distribution to other nodes\n\nPolicy distribution (step 1 above) and policy enforcement (steps 4\u20135) are **decoupled**. The K8s watcher on each node independently updates the local `Repository`. A compilation failure in `ReloadDatapath()` on node A returns an error only to node A's `regenerateBPF()` call. Node B's watcher continues to receive CNP updates from the API server, and node B's `regenerateBPF()` runs independently in node B's process. There is no shared compilation state, no distributed lock, and no cross-node signaling in the compilation path.\n\nPer-node policy status is tracked independently via `CiliumNetworkPolicyNodeStatus` (`pkg/k8s/apis/cilium.io/v2/cnp_types.go` lines 90\u201396): each node reports its own `OK` and `Enforcing` fields to the CNP status subresource, so a failure on one node is visible in the CNP status without affecting other nodes' enforcement.\n\n---\n\n## Q4: eBPF Map Scoping and State Isolation\n\n### Are eBPF maps node-local or cluster-wide?\n\neBPF maps are **strictly node-local**. They exist in the kernel of the node where they were created. There is no mechanism for eBPF maps to span multiple nodes.\n\n### BPF filesystem pinning and namespaces\n\nMaps are pinned to the BPF filesystem (bpffs) on each node:\n\n- **`bpf.TCGlobalsPath()`** (`pkg/bpf/bpffs_linux.go` lines 49\u201354): Returns `<bpffs>/tc/globals` (default: `/sys/fs/bpf/tc/globals`). Global maps like `cilium_lxc` (lxcmap), `cilium_call_policy`, and `cilium_egresscall_policy` are pinned here.\n\n- **`bpf.CiliumPath()`** (`pkg/bpf/bpffs_linux.go` lines 56\u201360): Returns `<bpffs>/cilium`. Per-endpoint and per-device directories are created under this path.\n\n- **Per-endpoint directories**: `bpffsEndpointDir()` (`pkg/datapath/loader/paths.go` lines 63\u201365) returns `/sys/fs/bpf/cilium/endpoints/<endpoint-id>`. Per-endpoint bpf_link objects (for TCX attachment) are pinned in `bpffsEndpointLinksDir()` (lines 73\u201375).\n\n- **Per-device directories**: `bpffsDeviceDir()` (`paths.go` lines 29\u201336) returns `/sys/fs/bpf/cilium/devices/<device-name>`.\n\n- **Per-endpoint policy maps**: Named `cilium_policy_v2_<id>` (from `policymap.MapName = \"cilium_policy_v2_\"`, `pkg/maps/policymap/policymap.go` line 34). The path is constructed by `bpf.LocalMapPath(policymap.MapName, e.ID)` (`pkg/endpoint/bpf.go` line 88), which resolves to `/sys/fs/bpf/tc/globals/cilium_policy_v2_<id>`. `policymap.OpenOrCreate(path)` (lines 487\u2013491) creates or opens this map on the local node only.\n\n- **Global call maps**: `cilium_call_policy` and `cilium_egresscall_policy` (program arrays, `policymap.go` lines 25\u201329) are created by `policymap.InitCallMaps()` (lines 514\u2013536) on each node independently.\n\n- **lxcmap** (`cilium_lxc`): A node-local hash map (`pkg/maps/lxcmap/lxcmap.go` lines 36\u201348) mapping endpoint IPs to endpoint metadata. Written by `lxcmap.WriteEndpoint()` (`pkg/endpoint/bpf.go` line 473).\n\nThe bpffs is mounted per-node (each Linux kernel has its own `/sys/fs/bpf` namespace). The `CheckOrMountFS()` function (`pkg/bpf/bpffs_linux.go` lines 295\u2013301) mounts bpffs on the local node at startup.\n\n### How a map failure on one node affects other nodes\n\nIt does not. The document `/logs/agent/investigation.md` answers all four questions with specific file paths, function names, and line references drawn directly from the `github.com/sg-evals/cilium--a2f97aa8` repository.\n\n**Key findings:**\n\n**Q1 \u2013 Per-Node eBPF Lifecycle:** The `loader` struct (`pkg/datapath/loader/loader.go`) drives compilation via `compile()` in `compile.go`, which invokes `clang` with node-specific flags: CPU ISA from `getBPFCPU()` (probing `probes.HaveV3ISA()`/`HaveV2ISA()`), CPU count from `ebpf.PossibleCPU()`, and node-specific headers written by `writeNodeConfigHeader()` / `writeNetdevHeader()`. The program becomes node-local at `bpf.LoadAndAssign()` in `reloadEndpoint()`, which issues the `bpf(BPF_PROG_LOAD)` syscall to the local kernel.\n\n**Q2 \u2013 Deployment Architecture:** Cilium runs as a DaemonSet (one `cilium-agent` per node). Failures are contained by: (1) `realizeBPFState()` returning errors locally, (2) `LogStatus(BPF, Failure, ...)` marking only the local endpoint, and (3) `startRegenerationFailureHandler()` retrying locally. The `compilationLock` is a node-local `RWMutex` with no cross-node effect.\n\n**Q3 \u2013 Policy Distribution vs. Enforcement:** Each node independently watches CNP/CCNP/KNP via `startK8sPolicyWatcher()` (`pkg/policy/k8s/cell.go`). The pipeline `Repository \u2192 policyCache \u2192 selectorPolicy.DistillPolicy() \u2192 regenerateBPF() \u2192 policyMapSync()` is entirely per-node. A compilation failure on one node returns an error only to that node's `regenerateBPF()` \u2014 other nodes' watchers and compilers run independently.\n\n**Q4 \u2013 eBPF Map Scoping:** All maps are node-local, pinned to the node's bpffs (`/sys/fs/bpf`). `TCGlobalsPath()` \u2192 `/sys/fs/bpf/tc/globals` (global maps), `LocalMapPath()` \u2192 per-endpoint policy maps, `bpffsEndpointDir()` \u2192 per-endpoint bpf_link pins. A map failure on one node affects only that node's endpoint regeneration; other nodes' maps live in separate kernel instances."
}
